La photo est magique, terriblement belle et chargée d'émotions.<br>Je ressors de sa cabane, toute émue et dans l'espoir de pouvoir montrer une telle image aux générations suivantes à mon tour.

Post_ID: 1887257593823522543	|Post_Code: Bow4shPgm7v	|Owner_ID: 11323592	|Likes: 1372	|Time_Stamp: 1539198658	|Tags: []	|Caption: DAY 183 • MILE 2,190.9 // THE END<br>.<br>I DID IT!!! 🤯 I just completed my thru hike of the Appalachian Trail - trekking 2,190 miles from Georgia to Maine! On April 8th I left Amicalola Falls headed North, and exactly 6 months later on October 8th I summited Mount Katahdin. Bringing an end to an incredible adventure<br>.<br>I shivered through snow and cold nights. Hiked through continuous days of rain (when you forget what it’s like to be dry). Trudged through mud and flooded trail. I climbed and crawled up mountains of sheer rock, stumbling and falling down the other side. Evaded bears, rattlesnakes, and ticks. I was chased and caught by thunderstorms that left me scared and vulnerable. Injured my achilles, rolled my ankles, and had endless blisters that almost took me off trail. It’s been a rollercoaster of physical and mental challenges that left me feeling broken at times. I cried and cursed the trail but the memories and friends I’ve made over the past 14 states weighs heavier than all those crazy struggles. I couldn’t have done this without my trail family, the trail angels, everyone who supported the Kickstarter!, my family and friends off trail, and you guys! Everyone on here who cheered me on, sent me supportive messages, commented moving and inspiring words on my posts, and even shared my journey with your friends. It’s emotional to think how amazing everyone has been - you all kept me walking when I couldn’t find the motivation. I can’t thank you enough. A decade-long dream of mine came true. It’s gonna take me a minute to process this...

Post_ID: 1877242216704830765	|Post_Code: BoNTdmcDu0t	|Owner_ID: 459064939	|Likes: 125	|Time_Stamp: 1538004732	|Tags: []	|Caption: When I started on the trail my goal was to finish as fast as I could, just go go go, more miles more miles, just get to Maine. <br>I talked to my dad one afternoon on a stop for a snack, and he said "whatever you do out there, make sure you have fun." Those words didn't really hit me until one of my more difficult days, I listened to John Mayer's, Why Georgia, and for some reason the phrase "Am I living it right?" just smacked me in the face... I immediately sat down on the side of the trail and reflected... "Am I enjoying this?  What did success look like to me out here?" I love hiking, but I hadn't stopped to take a single picture of any flowers that day, I hadn't stopped to chat with hikers I had passed along the trail, because the only thing I was concerned about was more and more miles. <br>I decided then that I was going to make it more about enjoying myself, even if that meant putting in less miles in a day.<br><br>Everything was going great until I came off the trail for a weekend and tore both of my rotator cuffs. I went back on the trail, after less than the recommended doctors rest, and then I hurt one of my shoulders again while throwing my pack on and had to stay in a hostel for a few days.  I then went back on the trail and got very sick.  I felt like I couldn't catch a break.  But I was truly just so happy to be out in the woods on a hiking adventure and I knew it was all going to be ok. ⛰️❤️ One of my biggest personality challenges is being a stickler when it comes to plans.  From the beginning, this Grand Adventure has tested me.  From being late to getting on the trail, to the everyday thing that wasn't going right while hiking.  I continued to remind myself I just needed to roll with the punches. <br>My original goal was to be done with the Appalachian Trail by the time I had to leave for Africa... Well the trail plan changed and the Africa plan was moved up, so God continued to remind me, just go with it.<br><br>Now I'm at the airport in Charleston and our flight has been delayed over 4 hours.  So again, God continues to remind me, roll with the punches and it will all work out. ❤️ Am I living it right?... Well, I'm trying. ❤️

The @appalachiantrail was such a rollercoaster. Mentally and physically it pushed me to the very brink. None of my previous hikes brutalized me this way. It was absolutely sadistic at times - had me schlepping through miles of pure rock, tripping over roots, bouldering up sheer mountain faces - I got scraped and stabbed; ended up face planting in the dirt more times than I can count; I screamed and cried and cursed the gods for putting me through such hell - and just as many times I laughed my ass off with my incredible trail family - @rebecca.harnish, @moronman, @austincolelambert_jinx, @garrettvandeperre and Crypto - creating ridiculous inside jokes throughout the course of 14 states. And that's pretty damn impossible to imagine, especially now that this incredible adventure is over. To all you beautiful souls I met on this wild ride - thank you for sharing your stories and your love with me. To all my friends and family who supported me through this - I can't thank you enough. Words cannot describe my strong feelings of affection for this trail and the amazing people who inhabited it this spring/summer. You made my journey spectacular; I hope our paths cross again soon. For some reason, I got a good feeling this isn't my last thru hike 😏⠀<br>.⠀<br>.⠀<br>AT thru hike ⠀<br>127 days (March 20 - July 24)⠀<br>2190.9 miles"⠀<br>.⠀<br>.⠀<br>.⠀<br>.⠀<br>#guthookguides #backpacking #thetrek #optoutside #hiking #mountains #at2018 #thruhike #atthruhike #hikerlife #atnobo2018 #keepitwild #getoutside #neverstopexploring #hiketheat #dirtbag #hikerlife #traillife #rei1440project #gossamergear #maine #katahdin ⠀<br>📷: @danbrownontrail

Franconia Ridge was gorgeous and we have been so fortunate to have excellent weather for the days we have summited. The AT only lends itself to summiting Washington and Madison but in our excitement we went up and over Eisenhower, too. Last night we did a work for stay at the Madison Springs hut. The crew was so fun, and we had a terrific meal and washed dishes and scraped the freezer of ice in return for the meal and the opportunity to sleep inside. This hut has the best sunset and sunrise views and was the first of the huts to be built by the AMC in the White’s. Today we climbed up and over Mt Madison and down through Pinkham Notch and then back up and over the Wildcats and then back down near the Carter Notch hut where we met a few of the hut crew and had a hearty bowl of stew and some delicious treats compliments of the hut master. Post_ID: 1780635121793385056	|Post_Code: Bi2FjWFFEJg	|Owner_ID: 5724497835	|Likes: 266	|Time_Stamp: 1526488269	|Tags: []	|Caption: AT Day 58- Mile 863.0<br>Waynesboro- I woke up and finished the miles I didn’t finish the day before. You can read about it in the last post. After packing up camp, we headed off to Walmart for me to buy a T-shirt. 850 Miles on backpacking and I didn’t carry or use a T-shirt. The nice weather days have me hiking without a shirt but I’m getting a rash in some areas my back from the sweat and my pack rubbing my skin. I’ll use body glide and hope a shirt will offer a buffet and relief. Putting on the new blue shirt felt weird. I’ve been in the same exact clothing from the beginning. Everyday i put on the same socks, same shorts, same shoes, and all my needed possessions are on my back. I’ve swapped a few pieces of gear and gotten rid of items that I no longer needed, but adding anything new, especially clothing is strange. It did feel nice though! We then grabbed breakfast before heading into Shenandoah. Since I completed about 14 miles early morning, we decided to drive into SNP and not do any hiking today. We handed out some fruit and apple pie bars to hikers as trail magic on another hot and humid day. I ran into a few hikers I knew and got to meet others. Fruit is always a hit for trail magic! We then set up camp and enjoyed a campfire and @daniel.woody made some awesome dinner. It was finally an early night to bed and getting some rest my body and legs long for. My hiking thoughts have become more consistent and I’m struggling with a few things mentally. I’m trying to work through them and talk/share with my girlfriend about the struggles. I’ve always been a person to not ask for help and try to do everything on my own. In my depression, that tends to drive me deeper into a hole. Since meeting Kari, I try to share everything I can so she understands me almost as well as I understand me, if not better. Hiking brings me happiness and a peace that I can’t find in the busy world. It’s my escape to work through my issues and focus on positives. I’m trusting things will work themselves out even if it’s not what I have planned.... I’ll share more in the next few days. But thanks for following and I’m glad I could be a vessel for y’all to share this journey.

Post_ID: 1777652569398891370	|Post_Code: BirfZftFNNq	|Owner_ID: 5724497835	|Likes: 358	|Time_Stamp: 1526132721	|Tags: []	|Caption: AT Day 54- Mile 786.0<br>Bearwallow Gap to US 501- 35.2 Mile Day.<br>Wow what a day! My first 30+ mile day went late into the night. The morning started with me saying goodbye to my girlfriend and hitting the trail. The first few hours I was so lost in thoughts and emotions that I forgot I was even backpacking. For me, Hiking has always been a great way to spend time in thought and meditation. When in nature, you no longer feel like king of the jungle (as a human we are superior beings). Rather, you feel like you fit in and belong. The oxygen we breath in from the plants, in turn giving them carbon dioxide. The bugs and animals and birds don’t seem to mind that I’m walking through the woods, instead I am part of them out here. We find shelter, we find food, and we drink water. That’s how simple life has become out here. <br>Around the 9 mile mark, I came across a swimming hole. With temps now in upper 80s and not a cloud to be found, I dove in on this opportunity. My feet and ankles hurt badly every day so the cold rushing water is the best therapy I can do. There was sign posted for free shuttle to get burgers and shakes so of course I called. The owner of Middle Creek Campground came down and picked me up and drove me the short 1.5 miles to the campground. Other hikers got the same idea, escape the heat and get a treat. Note to future hikers... definitely stop there. A meal midday is game changing and not having to walk off trail is even better. They cater to hikers and you can even camp, swim or do laundry there. I got back to the trail but not before one last leg soak. The afternoon started with 1100’ climb up and over Fork Mountain, followed by 2300’ climb up Floyd Mountain. Once again I hiked topless as the sweat gushed from me. Luckily water sources weren’t a problem to find today and I was able to pound a liter at most places. The early evening was filled with hiking through the green tunnel that is now in full bloom. After climbing over Apple Orchard Mountain, the trail is down hill. I knew I wanted to do a big day since I was well rested and had a couple lower mileage days in the last week. *** continued in comments ***

A few sections had bars for people to climb but it clearly wasn’t needed for any real hiker (built for tourist). Post_ID: 1773273314821548205	|Post_Code: Bib7q9Dniit	|Owner_ID: 5724497835	|Likes: 276	|Time_Stamp: 1525610673	|Tags: ['#trailmagic']	|Caption: AT Day 48 Mile 695.6<br>Laurel Creek Shelter to Trout Creek VA 620- 21.3 Mile Day- I somehow got my tent up last night before the rain came. I passed out quickly and woke up just before 3am. Normally I go back to sleep but today, my anxious self jumped up and got my day started. My ankle was tight from yesterday’s twisting and I planned to do a simple 14 Miles to a road crossing, then hitch up to Daleville. Once in Daleville, I would check into the hotel and wait for my girlfriend to arrive from Delaware. I packed up and got the hike started under dark, cloudy skies and the view of my headlamp. The temp was around 50 so made for a great early morning. The hours rolled by and so did the miles. I could notice my ankle but instead, I shifted my thoughts to other things like the anticipation of my lady’s arrival! I passed the 14 mile mark around sunrise and knew there was another road ahead 7 more miles. Onward I went without needing much water or food. In the last few miles, the overcompensation for my left ankle began to set in. My left shin started hurting, then calf felt like it was going to cramp, my knee began to throb and eventually it worked it’s way up to my left butt cheek. All of the pain was tolerable but noticeable. I finished on a gravel road and hiked out to the pave one. Once there I caught a hitch and figured my day was pretty much over. A nap at the hotel and some food was my new focus. As luck would have it, this section of actually takes a southern turn, and I was hitching on the wrong side of the road. The ride that picked me up, took me back the way I can towards Newport VA (a town with a post office and a gas station). I got dropped off an hour south of where my hotel reservations were! I grabbed a chocolate milk, Gatorade, banana and apple pie as i tried to figure out what to do. Luckily a previous Thru Hiker said she could help me out! @lindsayeclark Picked me up and drove me the 30+ miles to Daleville! THANK YOU!! #trailmagic I grabbed a coffee, BBQ, a nap and about 17 showers to try and smell not homeless. My love arrived and we had a great time catching up over a beer and fried Brussels sprouts at Ballast Point Brewery. 🖤

Post_ID: 1772556084810524907	|Post_Code: BiZYl4jlqjr	|Owner_ID: 5724497835	|Likes: 231	|Time_Stamp: 1525525173	|Tags: []	|Caption: AT Day 47 674.3<br>Pine Swamp to Laurel Creek Shelter-18.5Mile Day. The miles are starting to stack up and my legs feel good. The climbs in the morning don’t bother me much. Today’s quick 700’ climb over a mile seemed easy even with the sun beating down. Early in the morning, the sweat began to pour and it never stopped unless I took a break. But taking a break means that the little annoying bugs are all around your face. However, on these hot days, water stops or a brief moment in shade is worth it. After stopping for a quick lunch, I pressed on at a causal pace, not trying to exert too much energy. Then it happened... without warning my left foot hit something and my ankle rolled. This happens normally at least once a day and you just walk it off. But this one felt different. I quickly stopped, tied my shoe as tight as possible and hiked on. I came to a stream within an few miles and soaked the ankle and foot in the cold rushing water. No signs of swelling but I could feel everything getting tight. I grabbed the emergency duct tape from around my lighter, taped my ankle, tied my shoe extra tight and hiked towards Kelly Knob. The pain was manageable and I was doing alright. As i started my final climb for the day, the clouds behind me revealed themselves as i reached higher elevation. My clear day and picture perfect skies would soon be wind gust and rain clouds. I tried to out run the storm, but even with a good left leg, that wasn’t going to happen. I got into the shelter just after Kelly Knob as the rain really began to come down. I set up my tent, ate some food, and laid on my pad with my legs elevated. I can feel a difference between my good leg and bad one but still don’t see swelling. I have a short 14 mile day tomorrow before meeting up with my girlfriend and taking a zero. A little rest and ice should get be back feeling 💯 on Monday!

If you are passing though Pearisburg, plan on staying there! It’s much nicer than the 2 motels. It’s ran by Thru hikers who actually care about your needs and wants. Post_ID: 1771041799676488618	|Post_Code: BiUASIoFeuq	|Owner_ID: 5724497835	|Likes: 328	|Time_Stamp: 1525344656	|Tags: []	|Caption: AT Day 45- Mile 635.4<br>Dismal Falls to VA 634 Pearisburg- 24 Mile Day... waking up next to Dismal Falls was unreal. A flawless night to cowboy camp. It was a cold morning and I didn’t want to leave my quilt’s warmth. There was 24 miles between me and Pearisburg. I planned on doing all 24 but if I came up short, I would just camp and resupply in the morning. For once, I had enough food. The first 6-8 miles were beautiful as I hiked along streams and many foot bridges to cross them. Most of the morning was spent in shade. Then the climb came but I timed it to have it done before noon. The sun crept up and brought temps in the 80s. The next miles was hiking along the ridge line in the exposed sun. I went shirtless all day to avoid a sweat soaked shirt. For the most part it was an easy hike except the sun definitely drained me. That last 8 miles had essentially no water sources until the last 2 miles. It was a .2 off trail hike to a water source and I decided to press on into town. I was in shade for the remaining 2 miles but they were tough. Going down big stone steps made it feel like my knees were going to shatter. Each step just pounding the joints. When I start hiking in the mornings, each step is calculated and planned 3 steps early. I make sure my foot lands gently on the smoothest, softest surface. Later in the day, you can hear me coming a mile away. My feet barely clearing the rocks, often kicking a hidden root and trying not to fall from it. I twist each ankle about once a day on good days and 3-4 times each on bad ones. Good days only kick and trip on 5-6 rocks and roots. Bad ones, about 2 dozen. Somehow my feet remain healthy. My legs hurt from the hips down, but that’s not going to change. They hurt in the mornings, but once warmed up, they feel great. Not until the end of a long hiking day do I feel all the pains again. But it’s worth it.

Post_ID: 1770461347378988614	|Post_Code: BiR8TcTFYZG	|Owner_ID: 5724497835	|Likes: 386	|Time_Stamp: 1525275461	|Tags: []	|Caption: AT Day 44- Mile 611.4<br>US52 to Dismal Falls 21.2 Mile Day- I’m beginning to understand why they call it the Virginia Blues. Today, I crossed the 600 mile mark but these milestones are no longer worth celebrating. We’ve been in VA for over 100 miles already and the trail feels the same everyday. Silly climbs up and around mountains, all of which leads to no views and just down the other side. Then repeat. Trees and bushes block what would be the views of small towns and other mountains. You can sometimes catch an opening and steal a view but nothing to capture in a photo. However, the forest is starting to come alive as Spring finally arrives. The Mountain Laurel is beginning to bloom and makes the trail smell like fresh flowers. Other wild flowers are popping up and the trees beginning to bloom. If I don’t have views now, it will only get worse with foliage, but watching the transition from a dead forest to a life filled one is neat. There are more bird species than I can count and I continue to see wildlife. We hiked 19 miles to Trent’s Grocery and then .5 off the trail to get there. After a day in the high 70s, the AC and cold drinks were the first thing I went for. I grabbed a burger and chicken tenders and a few food items for resupply. I then caught a hitch back to the trail on a flatbed truck and hiked the remaining 2 miles to a blue blaze trail off the AT where we would camp for the night. Dismal Falls, .3 off the trail was a great spot! We cowboy camped out in the open on the rocks next to the falls. Laying there, we saw a massive shooting star and were treated to a great last visual before falling asleep.<br>Special shout out to my dude @jy_mabry and his daughter Willow! That would’ve been us had Jacob not helped out. He even took that hiker down into town to his hotel. We ended up setting up tents right off the trail head for the night and sat on the rock cliffs as trucks drove by US 77 down below. Falling asleep to sounds of a major highway isn’t the best but I’m in my tent, no rain fly, able to look up at the stars and almost full moon. It was a good day.

Bacon and I built a fire as Brick laid in the hammock reading. As for my new sleeping pad.... after first laying on it, I’d go through all that trouble again. It’s quite, soft, and weighs only 9.6oz. Brick and I slept in until about 9am. It felt great to get some sleep. That hasn’t happened in a few days. I woke up with sore calves for the first time all trip and my shins were tight as well. I grabbed a shower since we were still at the Church Hostel. Bacon, Brick and myself packed up and walked down to the road to hitch back to the trail. I’ve been the king of getting hitchs for us. Yesterday the 2 of them tried for 45 mins in the rain to no avail. I then went out to the road and got us a ride in a pick up truck in under 10 minutes. This has been typical for me through all towns (other than Gatlinburg). I even sometimes get cars to turn around and go back they way they came. It happened again yesterday. I’m also great at getting hitches out of gas stations and stores by just being friendly and asking to sit in a truck bed. Well, today.... I couldn’t get a hitch! We stood out there for over an hour in the cold and misty rain and not 1 person slowed down. I even tried my pathetic stranded face and nothing! As we watched rain clouds move in, Brick and I decided to call it a day and take our first 0 day in over 200 miles. We sat around the rest of the day just eating food and relaxing. We got a ride to the local general store another town over so we could get some real food instead of what we have in our packs. The sun poked out late afternoon and Brick was able to relax in his hammock for the first time since getting it mailed out. I enjoyed a few cold ones on the porch as I washed my socks and shorts in the spring and line dried them. The sun made a late day appearance indicating the next few days should be nice!

Reset night worked! I had a new outlook and all the support on social media inspired me. Thank you. This morning, I woke up and hopped in an epsom salt bath. I massaged out my sore leg muscles and could feel the toxins sweating out of my upper body and face. We then relaxed until about noon to allow the temps to rise slightly. After catching the free shuttle back to Massie Gap, Brick and I proceeded on to find the spot on the trail where we left off. The rain was blowing but the wind had died from 80 mph gust to 25, which was manageable. We questioned if we should’ve stayed in the room another night but as we climbed the mountain, we saw ponies! That changed everything for me. We took a few pictures and Brick hiked on. I stayed behind enjoying the ponies and followed them a bit off trail. As I continued on, I came across another herd with a baby. They were rolling around and playing and clearly liked today’s weather better than the last 2 days as well. The forest looked alive and more colorful than most days. I took time to stop and capture pictures and videos. As I hiked on, it became clear the trail was transitioning from a popular scenic spot into another connecting section. I picked up the pace and met Brick at a shelter. The trail once again was flowing like a river as the rain water rushed down the mountain. Many times, there was no option but walk through 6” plus of water and mud. We decided to do another 9 miles to Dickey Gap knowing there was a donation based hostel with a bunkhouse. Just as the trail crossed the road, it began to rain. A minute or 2 later, we caught a hitch and got dropped off at the Troutdale Church Hostel. Troutdale has a population of less than 100 with no actual businesses in the ‘town’. *** Continued in Comments***

Post_ID: 1764911826167299980	|Post_Code: Bh-OfR6ln-M	|Owner_ID: 5724497835	|Likes: 385	|Time_Stamp: 1524613906	|Tags: []	|Caption: AT Day 37- Mile 502.2<br>Thomas Knob Shelter to Massie Gap. 3.7 Mile Day- Today was the first day where real thoughts of quitting filled my head. Every day I think about quitting, sometimes multiple times a day. But that’s something every Thru Hiker experiences and the desire to push on always pushes out that negative thought. Today was tough. After climbing up to the shelter yesterday in some of the worst conditions, we woke up this morning in the same. The shelter felt like we were going to blow of the mountain as it shook in every gust. The rain pounded down on the tin roof like someone was dropping tons of marbles every second. My new sleeping pad, left my body feeling more stiff from the nights sleep than my longest day on trail did. Once again with no cell service, Brick and I read and reread the guidebooks trying to formulate a plan. We could wait out the storm in the shelter, but would run out of food and need to find a town. Neither of us had water for at least 12-15 hours. The spring was a couple hundred yards away and the idea of getting soaked for some water didn’t seem worth it at night. Now morning, I decided to make a run for it and grab 1 liter for us to share with breakfast meals. We had an option of going backwards, down trail for 4 miles to a road crossing and hope for a hitch. But the idea of backtracking only is appealing in emergency situations so we decided to trek forward. The guidebook said there was an Inn 6.8 Miles off trail from Massie Gap. The problem is, no map, no service, no idea of what road and direction. We reached the gap and a parking lot and didn’t see a single sign of humans. I remembered reading about a campground that didn’t open until May 1 but it had a courtesy phone so we walked down the road in that direction. Our main hope was a car would pass and we would be saved but no one was coming up to Grayson Highlands on a dirt road on a day like this. We reached a locked up general store and we just walked a few miles in the wrong direction. ***continued in comments***

As the wind intensified, the rain began to pour down. This seems all to familiar at this point. I heard and saw, 2 trees blow down in the woods. That’s a scary sound and you can feel it vibrate the ground. All day branches were falling taking my thoughts to weird places. As I climbed out of the woods, I began to climb the open face Bald of Whitetop. For the first time in my life, wind pushed me over. I literally hit the spot as the storm hit. The rain to the face gave me a brain freeze feeling. I considered stopping right after and setting up my tent to warm up and camp for the night but it was only noon and I pushed on. The day only got worse. I crossed VA 600 at Elk Garden and considered finding a hitch to get anywhere. Anywhere off the damn trail. I had no service and no clue what was around. A car passes and then another but I was hiding from the storm in the bathroom. I decided to make the last 4 mile climb from 4400’ to the shelter 5413’. With the extra elevation came more wind, rain and misery. This hike is one of the sections I was most looking forward to of my entire Thru and planned on slowing down to enjoy it. Today, I wished it was over and I was off the mountain. Once at the shelter, Brick and I had the top section to ourselves and 2 mice. I crawled in my quilt, laid on my shitty pad I just bought and regretted that decision quick! I was able to fall asleep by 5:30pm but woke up constantly more sore than before. The 2 things I tell people are the most important (your feet and your sleep) I fucked up. I’m on night 2 of terrible sleep. I sent my previous pad home because it was too insulated and made me sweat. Now I feel like I’m laying on nothing. (Continued in comments)

Part of my journey on this trail is to push myself both physically and mentally to points I haven’t experienced before to fully understand what I am capable of accomplishing. If we weren’t able to complete it in 3 days, no sweat. We have everything we need to set up camp and draw out the days. Around lunch, we arrived at Trail Magic and received burgers with egg, hot dogs, and more fixings and sides then we could imagine. Former 2014 thru hikers get their Trail Family together every year in that exact spot and whip up trail Magic for this years class. After an hour of hanging out, we made the final 15 mile push to town. Not going to lie, it sucked. The sun was blasting down on us and the previous 60 miles had taken their toll on my body. We hit the VA state line, leaving TN behind us! 3 states done! We will be in VA for over 500 miles, but there were only 3 down hill miles between me and real food! I love food! I looked at Brick, and he knew what was about to happen..... I took off running for the town! It wasn’t much of a run, more of an old man shuffle but I made it! Josh and Drew were waiting for us and we treated the boys to Pizza Dinner for their help. I wish I was more chatty but the miles and sun drained me. (Continued in comments)

Pun intended because we also plowed through snow, sometimes over our ankle, mud and flooded muddy trail. We climbed over Roan mountain as the wind tossed us around. Parts of the trail felt like kids were hiding and pelting us with snowballs and ice but it was just getting blown off the trees into our faces. Normally this section of trail is quite easy as the locals told us but today’s elements didn’t make it as simple as described. Nothing could stop us though. I hiked in my short shorts and just a midlayer and was able to stay warm all day except for my cold, wet feet and my hands. I don’t not regret sending my gloves home yet. After we finish Roan Mt, we got out of the trees and felt the sun! My feet warmed up despite every step being in water. As we climbed Round Bald and Jane Bald, we were granted a few views but enjoyed the sun and knew a shelter was close. One of the wind gust took my hat and sent it flying. Luckily I got it before I needed a new trail name. Over 800+ miles hiked in that hat and it never once came off. We arrived at a shelter and decided to push on 1.8 more miles to Overmountain Shelter. (If you saw IG story, you get it). Sure enough, the rain didn’t come at 10 am, but by 10:03am I was soaked. The trail changed to a river and thick mud. Luckily I was the first one on the trail that morning and didn’t have the slop the others behind me had to deal with. My rain jacket preformed flawlessly and kept my core/arms dry and warm. The 40 mph gust on top of the mountains tried its best to blow me off. At times, I could feel myself shifting off trail. The rain, felt like hail as it bashed me in the face. The remaining 2 hours were spent with my head straight down just finishing the miles. Finally I reached, Greasy Creek Gap where I was heading .6miles off trail to Greasy Creek Friendly to dry out and survive the night. There were no signs on the trail for the hostel, not allowed, so I trusted my instincts and guidebook and ventured down this sketchy unmarked side trail. Some parts were 6” of water over my ankles. I took a good spill and fell into a briar patch. Luckily no damage done surprisingly for how short my shorts are... 😂 ***CONTINUED IN COMMENTS***

The sound of the roaring river mixed with temps finally in the 40s at night, gave me great sleeping conditions. However, tonight, our spot is a little different! When we woke up, we got a ride back to Sams Gap where we left off yesterday. After 9 hours and 24 miles, we finally made it back to town and the river. The day was perfect- Sunshine, no clouds and 75 degrees. Bacon, Brick and myself summited Big Bald and took a long break to enjoy the views. Afterwards, we hiked the rest of the day at our own pace. By the time we got done, we laid in the grass at Uncle Johnny’s Hostel and drank a few sodas. No one wanted to set up tents, instead we hitched into town and grabbed BBQ. I mean after 24 mile day.... FOOD!!!!. When we got back to the River to finally set up camp, a group of people took our spot. It was 11pm and all we wanted was sleep after a long mileage and sun draining day. So, we picked this lovely location and called it home for the night. And yes, Bacon is under the picnic table (condensation on tent issue from the night before). Again temps in the 40s and I can still hear the river in the background..... just not quite the same view 😂 Also, im pretty much a pro at getting pickup trucks to pick up us Hitch Hikers. It’s a skill and an art form 🤙

Post_ID: 1747658319961947123	|Post_Code: BhA7fuGFnvz	|Owner_ID: 254241442	|Likes: 66	|Time_Stamp: 1522557128	|Tags: ['#smidgehikestheat', '#appalachiantrail2018', '#atthruhike2018', '#atnobo2018']	|Caption: Gear post 5 - Packing system<br><br>This is the majority of my stuff as I pack it into or strap it into sections of my pack. I find the Sea to Summit lightweight dry sacks to be helpful in keeping my crap organized. NOTE: I preemptively lined my green food dry sack with an oven roasting bag. I’m glad I did because the dry sack was NOT  waterproof when used as directed. Contents stayed dry but there was water between the layers after hanging on a bear cable overnight with rain. I also put my yellow quilt dry sack in an oven roasting back for extra protection. Made my pot cozy from Reflectix material purchased on Amazon, and used instructions online. It works ok- I actual prefer to use it as I eat out of my pot to help keep food warm longer. <br>#smidgehikestheat #appalachiantrail2018 #atthruhike2018 #atnobo2018
